<p><b>Robert Lewandowski</b> (<small>Polish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Polish" title="Help:IPA/Polish">[rbrt lvandfski]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-Robert_Lewandowski.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Pl-Robert_Lewandowski.ogg" class="internal" title="Pl-Robert Lewandowski.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; born 21 August 1988) is a Polish professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland national team</a>. He is renowned for his positioning, technique and finishing, and is widely regarded as one of the best strikers in the world, and one of the best players in Bundesliga history. He has scored over <a href="/wiki/List_of_men%27s_footballers_with_500_or_more_goals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of men&#39;s footballers with 500 or more goals">500 senior career goals</a> for club and country.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After being the top scorer in the third and second tiers of Polish football with <a href="/wiki/Znicz_Pruszk%C3%B3w" title="Znicz Pruszków">Znicz Pruszków</a>, Lewandowski moved to top-flight <a href="/wiki/Lech_Pozna%C5%84" title="Lech Pozna">Lech Pozna</a>, helping the team win the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Ekstraklasa" title="200910 Ekstraklasa">200910 Ekstraklasa</a>. In 2010, he transferred to <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, where he won honours including two consecutive <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesliga trophy">Bundesliga titles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bundesliga#Top_scorers" title="201314 Bundesliga">league's top goalscorer</a> award. In 2013, he also featured with Dortmund in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a>. Prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Bundesliga" title="201415 Bundesliga">201415 season</a>, Lewandowski agreed to join Dortmund's domestic rivals, Bayern Munich, on a <a href="/wiki/Free_transfer_(association_football)" title="Free transfer (association football)">free transfer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In Munich, he has won the Bundesliga title in each of his first six seasons. Lewandowski was integral in Bayern's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> win in <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201920 UEFA Champions League">201920</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>. He is one of only two players, alongside <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>, to achieve the European treble, while being the top scorer in all three competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-juni_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juni-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zet_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zet-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A full international for Poland since 2008, Lewandowski has earned over 110 caps and was a member of their team at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>. With 63 international goals, Lewandowski is the all-time top scorer for Poland. He won <a href="/wiki/IFFHS_World%27s_Best_International_Goal_Scorer" title="IFFHS World&#39;s Best International Goal Scorer">IFFHS World's Best International Goal Scorer Award</a> in 2015 and <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_%26_Statistics#IFFHS_World&#39;s_Best_Top_Goal_Scorer" title="International Federation of Football History &amp; Statistics">IFFHS World's Best Top Goal Scorer Award</a> in 2020. He has been named the <a href="/wiki/Pi%C5%82ka_no%C5%BCna_magazine_plebiscite" title="Pika nona magazine plebiscite">Polish Player of the Year</a> a record nine times.
</p><p>In 2020, Lewandowski won the <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Men%27s_Player" title="The Best FIFA Men&#39;s Player">Best FIFA Men's Player Award</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Men%27s_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="UEFA Men&#39;s Player of the Year Award">UEFA Men's Player of the Year Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He has been named to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="UEFA Team of the Year">UEFA Team of the Year</a> twice and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> Squad of the Season three times, and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers#All-time_top_scorers" title="List of UEFA Champions League top scorers">third-highest goalscorer</a> in the history of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski has been named the <a href="/wiki/Vereinigung_der_Vertragsfussballspieler" title="Vereinigung der Vertragsfussballspieler">VDV Bundesliga Player of the Season</a> a record four times. He has scored over 250 goals in the Bundesliga, having reached the century mark quicker than any other foreign player, and is the league's <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_records_and_statistics#Goals_2" title="Bundesliga records and statistics">all-time leading foreign goalscorer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, he has won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bundesliga_top_scorers_by_season" title="List of Bundesliga top scorers by season">Bundesliga top goalscorer award</a> in five seasons. Lewandowski was awarded four <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a> for the fastest five-goal haul in any major European football league since records have been kept, after scoring five times in nine minutes against <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">Wolfsburg</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:32%; ;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1012376600">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"  ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"  ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"When I was six, I remember <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Baggio" title="Roberto Baggio">Roberto Baggio</a> at the 1994 World Cup. When I was between 10 and 14, <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Del_Piero" title="Alessandro Del Piero">Alessandro Del Piero</a> was the best player for me. Then my idol was <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>. He was amazing  it wasn't just how he scored the goals but what he did for the team."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">Lewandowski on his childhood role models<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Lewandowski was born in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and grew up in <a href="/wiki/Leszno,_Warsaw_West_County" title="Leszno, Warsaw West County">Leszno, Warsaw West County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He took his first steps in football as an unregistered player for the local club, Partyzant Leszno.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, he joined MKS Varsovia Warsaw, where as a teen he played for seven years.<sup id="cite_ref-bajka_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bajka-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The following year he moved to Delta Warsaw, where he finally managed to play in the first team, scoring four goals.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 200607, Lewandowski was the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Second_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Second League">Polish third division</a>'s top goal scorer with 15 goals, helping <a href="/wiki/Znicz_Pruszk%C3%B3w" title="Znicz Pruszków">Znicz Pruszków</a> win promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-krol_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krol-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_II_liga_(Poland)" class="mw-redirect" title="200708 II liga (Poland)">next season</a> he was the top scorer in the <a href="/wiki/I_liga" title="I liga">Polish second division</a> with 21 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-krol_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krol-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lech_Pozna.C5.84"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lech_Pozna">Lech Pozna</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LewandowskiR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/LewandowskiR.jpg/170px-LewandowskiR.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/LewandowskiR.jpg/255px-LewandowskiR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2d/LewandowskiR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="331" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LewandowskiR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski, playing for <a href="/wiki/Lech_Pozna%C5%84" title="Lech Pozna">Lech Pozna</a>, was the top scorer of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Ekstraklasa" title="200910 Ekstraklasa">200910 Ekstraklasa</a>, with 18 goals.</div></div></div>
<p>In June 2008, <a href="/wiki/Lech_Pozna%C5%84" title="Lech Pozna">Lech Pozna</a> signed Lewandowski from Znicz for 1.5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty" title="Polish zoty">PLN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bajka_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bajka-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-official_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Earlier that month, Lewandowski's agent <a href="/wiki/Cezary_Kucharski" title="Cezary Kucharski">Cezary Kucharski</a> offered him to his former team <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Gij%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting Gijón">Sporting Gijón</a>, which had been promoted to the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Spanish top league</a> after ten years in the second tier. However, Sporting rejected him.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He debuted for Lech in July 2008 as a substitute in a first-round <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> qualifier versus <a href="/wiki/Khazar_Lankaran_FK" title="Khazar Lankaran FK">Khazar Lankaran</a> from <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>. In that match, he scored the only goal of the match. During his <a href="/wiki/Ekstraklasa" title="Ekstraklasa">Ekstraklasa</a> debut in the first game of the season in a match against <a href="/wiki/GKS_Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w" title="GKS Bechatów">GKS Bechatów</a>, he scored a heel flick goal just four minutes after coming into the game late second half. In <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Ekstraklasa" title="200809 Ekstraklasa">his first season</a> in the Polish top division, he was second in the goal-scoring charts. He finished the season with 18 goals in 42 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Lewandowski_»_Club_matches_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Lewandowski_»_Club_matches-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The next season, he became the top scorer with 18 goals and helped his team win the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Ekstraklasa" title="200910 Ekstraklasa">200910 championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Lewandowski_»_Club_matches_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Lewandowski_»_Club_matches-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>English coach, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Allardyce" title="Sam Allardyce">Sam Allardyce</a>, said that Lewandowski was about to join <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> in 2010, but the volcanic ash clouds caused by the <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallajökull">2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallajökull</a> which suspended all flights in and out of the UK, in addition to other financial worries, prevented the potential transfer.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, Lewandowski was also about to join Italian club <a href="/wiki/Genoa_C.F.C." title="Genoa C.F.C.">Genoa</a>, before president <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Preziosi" title="Enrico Preziosi">Enrico Preziosi</a> decided to cancel the transfer.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borussia_Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.932012:_Debut_season.2C_league_and_cup_double"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20102012:_Debut_season,_league_and_cup_double">20102012: Debut season, league and cup double</span></h4>
<p>Following press speculation that Lewandowski might move to one of a number of clubs,<sup id="cite_ref-republicca_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republicca-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blackburn_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blackburn-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> he joined <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> in June 2010, signing a four-year contract with the German club<sup id="cite_ref-officialborussia_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialborussia-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> for a fee reported to be worth around <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro"></a>4.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 19 September, he scored his first goal in the Bundesliga to make it 30 in the <a href="/wiki/Revierderby" title="Revierderby">Revierderby</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke 04</a>; the game ended 31.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 201112 Bundesliga campaign, Lewandowski profited from an injury of <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Barrios" title="Lucas Barrios">Lucas Barrios</a> and he was elevated to an ever-present position in the starting XI until the winter break. The striker responded by finding the net two times in Dortmund's 30 <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_DFB-Pokal#First_round" title="201112 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal first round</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/SV_Sandhausen" title="SV Sandhausen">SV Sandhausen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski opened his league account in a 20 win over <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a> on 20 August 2011 by providing the finishing touch from a <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a> cross.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October, Lewandowski provided an <a href="/wiki/Assist_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Assist (football)">assist</a> and netted a hat-trick in the club's 40 victory over <a href="/wiki/FC_Augsburg" title="FC Augsburg">FC Augsburg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> following a disappointing 30 loss to <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Olympique de Marseille</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201112 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He later scored his first Champions League goal in a 13 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a> on 19 October.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Dortmund climbed into second place in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Bundesliga" title="201112 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> with a comfortable 50 victory over <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a> on 22 October, with Lewandowski finding the net either side of half-time.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Dortmund travelled to <a href="/wiki/SC_Freiburg" title="SC Freiburg">SC Freiburg</a> on 17 December and Lewandowski struck twice and provided an assist for <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Gro%C3%9Fkreutz" title="Kevin Großkreutz">Kevin Großkreutz</a>, as Dortmund eased to a 41 triumph, scoring his first hat-trick in Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Due to his strong performances, he was named <a href="/wiki/Pi%C5%82ka_no%C5%BCna_magazine_plebiscite" title="Pika nona magazine plebiscite">Best Player of the Year in Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the winter break, on 22 January 2012, Dortmund thrashed <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> 51 to move level on points with leaders <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>; Lewandowski netted twice and added an assist for <a href="/wiki/Jakub_B%C5%82aszczykowski" title="Jakub Baszczykowski">Jakub Baszczykowski</a> in the rout.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> He scored in a 10 home win over Bayern Munich on 11 April.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The result gave Dortmund a six-point cushion over their title rivals with only four games left to play.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 21 April, Lewandowski provided the assist for <a href="/wiki/Shinji_Kagawa" title="Shinji Kagawa">Shinji Kagawa</a>'s 59th-minute goal as Dortmund won 20 over <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> to seal their second straight title.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In the final Bundesliga game of the campaign, Lewandowski scored two first-half goals as Dortmund beat Freiburg 40 and celebrated lifting the title.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski finished the year as the third top goal scorer with 22 goals, none from the penalty spot, and six assists.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the final game of the season for Dortmund, he scored a hat-trick in the <a href="/wiki/2012_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2012 DFB-Pokal Final">DFB-Pokal Final</a>, a 52 win over Bayern Munich, to earn the club its first league and cup double.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski finished as the DFB-Pokal's top goalscorer, with seven goals from six games.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.932014:_Champions_League_runner-up_and_league_top_goalscorer"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20122014:_Champions_League_runner-up_and_league_top_goalscorer">20122014: Champions League runner-up and league top goalscorer</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg/170px-Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg/255px-Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg/340px-Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="1050" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2013_in_Wilhelmshaven.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski playing for Dortmund in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_DFB-Pokal#First_round" title="201314 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> against <a href="/wiki/SV_Wilhelmshaven" title="SV Wilhelmshaven">Wilhelmshaven</a> in August 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Lewandowski made his first appearance of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Bundesliga" title="201213 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> campaign in Dortmund's 21 victory over <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a> on the opening day of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He netted his first goal in the 30 victory over <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> on 15 September 2012, extending Dortmund's run to 31 games unbeaten and moved the club into third in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, in the club's first <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201213 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> game of the season, Lewandowski netted an emphatic 87th-minute winner to defeat <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> by a score of 10.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He set club's new record of the longest scoring streak, having scored in 12 consecutive league games, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Friedhelm_Konietzka" title="Friedhelm Konietzka">Friedhelm Konietzka</a>'s record from <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Bundesliga" title="196465 Bundesliga">196465 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 9 February 2013, Lewandowski opened the scoring in a home match against Hamburger SV, but was sent off in the 31st minute for a foul on <a href="/wiki/Per_Ciljan_Skjelbred" title="Per Ciljan Skjelbred">Per Ciljan Skjelbred</a> and Dortmund lost 14. He finished season with 24 league goals, one goal short of the Bundesliga's topscorer, Bayer Leverkusen's <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Kie%C3%9Fling" title="Stefan Kießling">Stefan Kießling</a>.
</p><p>According to Borussia Dortmund director <a href="/wiki/Michael_Zorc" title="Michael Zorc">Michael Zorc</a>, speaking in February 2013, Lewandowski would not be renewing his contract with the club, and would leave either in the summer of 2013 or after the 201314 season.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 April 2013, Lewandowski became the first player to score <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_hat-tricks" title="List of UEFA Champions League hat-tricks">four goals in a Champions League</a> semi-final as Borussia Dortmund defeated Spanish champions <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid">Real Madrid</a> 41 in the first leg at BVB's <a href="/wiki/Westfalenstadion" title="Westfalenstadion">Westfalenstadion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 25 May, he played in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a> in which Borussia were defeated 21 by Bayern Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 July 2013, Lewandowski won the <a href="/wiki/2013_DFL-Supercup" title="2013 DFL-Supercup">2013 German Super Cup</a> with Dortmund 42 against Bayern Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_German_Super_Cup_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_German_Super_Cup-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal of the season in Dortmund's 40 win over Augsburg in the club's opening Bundesliga match on 10 August.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November, he scored his only hat-trick of the season in a 61 Bundesliga win against <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 February 2014, Lewandowski scored twice in <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201314 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> round-of-16 first-leg against <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a>, becoming BVB's overall top scorer in European competition, surpassing <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Chapuisat" title="Stéphane Chapuisat">Stéphane Chapuisat</a>'s 16 goals record.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He scored his 100th goal for the club on his 182nd appearance, as Dortmund defeated <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">VfL Wolfsburg</a> in the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> on 16 April 2014, and revealed a shirt with the number 100 in celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski ended the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Borussia_Dortmund_season" title="201314 Borussia Dortmund season">201314 season</a> as the top goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bundesliga" title="201314 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> with 20 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He also scored six goals in the Champions League, as Borussia reached the quarter-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> During the second leg of the round of 16 match between Borussia Dortmund and Zenit, Lewandowski received a second yellow card which resulted in him being suspended for the first leg of the quarter-final against Real Madrid.
</p><p>Lewandowski played his final match for Dortmund in the <a href="/wiki/2014_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2014 DFB-Pokal Final">2014 German Cup final</a> against Bayern Munich on 17 May. Manager <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="Jürgen Klopp">Jürgen Klopp</a> had excused him from some training ahead of the final due to injury concerns; although Lewandowski played all 120 minutes of the final, Dortmund lost 20.<sup id="cite_ref-Sixteen_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sixteen-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with 28 goals in 48 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_German_Super_Cup_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_German_Super_Cup-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bayern_Munich">Bayern Munich</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.932017:_Collective_and_individual_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20142017:_Collective_and_individual_success">20142017: Collective and individual success</span></h4>
<p>In November 2013, Lewandowski confirmed he would sign a pre-contractual agreement for Borussia Dortmund's rivals <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> which officially happened on 3 January 2014; signing a five-year contract, joining the team at the start of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="201415 FC Bayern Munich season">201415 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski was officially presented as a Bayern Munich player on 9 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Lewandowski_expects_to_win_many_titles_as_Pole_is_unveiled_at_Bayern_Munich_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Lewandowski_expects_to_win_many_titles_as_Pole_is_unveiled_at_Bayern_Munich-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201415_season">201415 season</span></h5>
<p>Pre-season started on 9 July 2014<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> at which time he was presented.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Lewandowski_expects_to_win_many_titles_as_Pole_is_unveiled_at_Bayern_Munich_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Lewandowski_expects_to_win_many_titles_as_Pole_is_unveiled_at_Bayern_Munich-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He made his preseason debut on 21 July 2014, scoring a goal in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On 6 August, he opened the scoring as Bayern contested the <a href="/wiki/2014_MLS_All-Star_Game" title="2014 MLS All-Star Game">2014 MLS All-Star Game</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>, eventually losing 12.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CSKA-Bavaria_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/CSKA-Bavaria_%284%29.jpg/160px-CSKA-Bavaria_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/CSKA-Bavaria_%284%29.jpg/240px-CSKA-Bavaria_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/55/CSKA-Bavaria_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CSKA-Bavaria_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski playing in the Champions League against <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> in October 2014</div></div></div>
<p>He made his competitive debut for his new club in a 20 loss to Borussia Dortmund in the <a href="/wiki/2014_DFL-Supercup" title="2014 DFL-Supercup">2014 German Super Cup</a> on 13 August 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-2014_German_Super_Cup_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_German_Super_Cup-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and scored his first goal in a 11 draw against Schalke 04 in his second league match on 30 August.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On 21 October, Lewandowski scored his first Champions League goal with Bayern Munich in a 71 away win against <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November, in his first league match against Dortmund, Lewandowski scored in a 21 win which put Bayern four points clear at the top of the table while leaving his former club in a relegation play-off place.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In his third match of the season against Dortmund on 4 April 2015, Lewandowski scored in the 36th minute in a 10 win.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He had scored after <a href="/wiki/Roman_Weidenfeller" title="Roman Weidenfeller">Roman Weidenfeller</a> "parried" <a href="/wiki/Thomas_M%C3%BCller" title="Thomas Müller">Thomas Müller</a>'s shot.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 February 2015, Lewandowski scored twice in Bayern's 60 win away at <a href="/wiki/SC_Paderborn_07" title="SC Paderborn 07">SC Paderborn 07</a>, his second goal of the game was his 10th of the league season.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> He scored twice in the first half on 21 April as Bayern overturned a deficit from the first leg to defeat <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">FC Porto</a> 74 on aggregate and advance to the semi-finals of the Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Five days later, after VfL Wolfsburg lost to <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>, Bayern won the Bundesliga title.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On 28 April, he scored again in a DFB-Pokal semi-final against Dortmund, opening a 11 draw which ended in Bayern's elimination via a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shootout</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> With 17 goals in 31 games, Lewandowski was joint-second highest scorer of the Bundesliga season alongside teammate <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Meier" title="Alexander Meier">Alexander Meier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with 25 goals in 49 appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_German_Super_Cup_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_German_Super_Cup-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201516_season">201516 season</span></h5>
<p>Lewandowski's second season began with the <a href="/wiki/2015_DFL-Supercup" title="2015 DFL-Supercup">German Super Cup</a> on 1 August, with Bayern losing in a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shootout</a> away to VfL Wolfsburg; he had been substituted in the 72nd minute for <a href="/wiki/Rafinha_(footballer,_born_1985)" title="Rafinha (footballer, born 1985)">Rafinha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-supercup_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supercup-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Eight days later in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_DFB-Pokal#First_round" title="201516 DFB-Pokal">first round of the DFB-Pokal</a>, he scored the last goal in a 31 win against <a href="/wiki/Oberliga_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Oberliga Baden-Württemberg">Oberliga Baden-Württemberg</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_N%C3%B6ttingen" title="FC Nöttingen">FC Nöttingen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August, in the opening match of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Bundesliga" title="201516 Bundesliga">new Bundesliga season</a>, he scored the second goal of a 50 win over Hamburg.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 September 2015, Lewandowski set a <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_records_and_statistics#Goals_2" title="Bundesliga records and statistics">Bundesliga record</a> by coming on as a substitute with Bayern trailing 01 to Wolfsburg and scoring five goals in 8 minutes and 59 seconds, the fastest by any player in Bundesliga history, to take a 51 lead. He also set Bundesliga records for the fastest <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> (three goals in four minutes), and most goals scored by a substitute (five).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski's five goals in nine minutes was also the fastest in any major European football league since <a href="/wiki/Opta_Sports" title="Opta Sports">Opta</a> began keeping records, and it ended Wolfsburg's 14-match unbeaten run.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He was awarded four certificates by <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a> for this feat.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Four days later, he scored twice in a 30 win at <a href="/wiki/1._FSV_Mainz_05" title="1. FSV Mainz 05">1. FSV Mainz 05</a>, the first goal being his 100th Bundesliga goal on his 168th appearance, a league record for a foreign player. He also reached 10 goals in the opening 7 matches with this brace, a feat only done before by <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September, he scored a <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_hat-tricks" title="List of UEFA Champions League hat-tricks">Champions League hat-trick</a> in a 50 win over <a href="/wiki/Dinamo_Zagreb" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinamo Zagreb">Dinamo Zagreb</a>, putting him on ten goals in three games in a week.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> He added two in a 51 rout of Dortmund five days later, to total 12 goals in his last four appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On 24 October, Lewandowski scored in a 40 home win over 1. FC Köln, a result which made Bayern the first Bundesliga team ever to win all 10 of their opening games of a season.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The victory in Cologne was also Bayern's 1,000th win in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On 11 January 2016, he achieved fourth place at the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="2015 FIFA Ballon d&#39;Or">2015 FIFA Ballon d'Or</a> awards.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 March 2016, Lewandowski scored the only goal in a 10 win against Köln<sup id="cite_ref-1._FC_Koln_0_1_Bayern_Munich_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1._FC_Koln_0_1_Bayern_Munich-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> to bring his league total up to 25 goals; a new personal best.<sup id="cite_ref-1._FC_Koln_0_1_Bayern_Munich_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1._FC_Koln_0_1_Bayern_Munich-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> He had scored 24 goals for Borussia Dortmund during the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Borussia_Dortmund_season" title="201213 Borussia Dortmund season">201213 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> His goal against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> on 3 May in the second leg of Bayern's Champions League semi-final exit saw him end the season's competition with nine goals.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 May 2016, Lewandowski scored both goals for Bayern in a 21 win at <a href="/wiki/FC_Ingolstadt_04" title="FC Ingolstadt 04">FC Ingolstadt</a> to confirm the Bavarian club as <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">champions of Germany</a> for the fourth consecutive season.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he scored his 30th goal of the season in Bayern's final league match of the season at home to <a href="/wiki/Hannover_96" title="Hannover 96">Hannover 96</a>. This made him the first foreign player to score 30 goals in the Bundesliga, the first player since <a href="/wiki/Dieter_M%C3%BCller" title="Dieter Müller">Dieter Müller</a> in <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_Bundesliga" title="197677 Bundesliga">197677</a>, and secured him the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bundesliga_top_scorers" title="List of Bundesliga top scorers">Torjägerkanone</a> for the second time in three seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with 42 goals in 51 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-supercup_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supercup-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201617_season">201617 season</span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="201617 FC Bayern Munich season">201617 season</a> started with Bayern winning the <a href="/wiki/2016_DFL-Supercup" title="2016 DFL-Supercup">2016 German Super Cup</a> on 14 August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_German_Super_Cup_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_German_Super_Cup-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On 19 August, in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_DFB-Pokal#First_round" title="201617 DFB-Pokal">first round of the DFB-Pokal</a>, Bayern defeated <a href="/wiki/FC_Carl_Zeiss_Jena" title="FC Carl Zeiss Jena">Carl Zeiss Jena</a> 50 with the help of Lewandowski's hat trick during the first half.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> He also assisted <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Vidal" title="Arturo Vidal">Arturo Vidal</a>'s goal in the seventy-second minute.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski opened the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Bundesliga" title="201617 Bundesliga">201617 Bundesliga</a> season with a hat trick in a 60 victory against Werder Bremen.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On 13 December, Lewandowski signed a new contract with Bayern, keeping him at the club until 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg/170px-Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg/255px-Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg/340px-Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2387" data-file-height="3535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_Training_2017-03_FC_Bayern_Muenchen-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski in training in March 2017</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 March 2017, Lewandowski reached 100 goals for Bayern in his 137th appearance for the club, scoring twice in a 30 victory against <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with 42 goals in 47 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_German_Super_Cup_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_German_Super_Cup-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.93present:_Back-to-back-to-back_Golden_Boots_and_Sextuple_win"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017present:_Back-to-back-to-back_Golden_Boots_and_Sextuple_win">2017present: Back-to-back-to-back Golden Boots and Sextuple win</span></h4>
<h5><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201718_season">201718 season</span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="201718 FC Bayern Munich season">season</a> began with Bayern Munich winning the <a href="/wiki/2017_DFL-Supercup" title="2017 DFL-Supercup">2017 German Super Cup</a> against Borussia Dortmund. Lewandowski scored the opening goal for Bayern by controlling a low cross from <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Kimmich" title="Joshua Kimmich">Joshua Kimmich</a> to cancel out <a href="/wiki/Christian_Pulisic" title="Christian Pulisic">Christian Pulisic's</a> opener. The match ended 22 after extra time. Lewandowski again scored the first penalty of the shootout as Bayern eventually won 54 to win the super cup.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski started from where he left in the last season and once again was the top scorer in the early stages of the Bundesliga. On 13 December 2017, in the league fixture against 1. FC Köln, he scored the only goal of the game to reach the top ten of goalscorers in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> A couple of months later, on <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Bundesliga" title="201718 Bundesliga">Matchday 22</a>, Lewandowski again found the back of the net against Schalke 04 at <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a> to equal the record of scoring in 11 successive home games in a single season, a record also held by then Bayern manager <a href="/wiki/Jupp_Heynckes" title="Jupp Heynckes">Jupp Heynckes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He continued his goal scoring form by scoring a hat-trick against Hamburger SV as the runaway leaders won 60, while he also missed a kick from the spot which would have been his fourth goal of the day. This was his first penalty missed for Bayern in the Bundesliga, nevertheless he scored the second spot kick to complete his hat-trick.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 February 2018, Lewandowski was voted Poland's Footballer of the Year for the seventh time in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> On 22 February 2018, Lewandowski fired his long-time agent, <a href="/wiki/Cezary_Kucharski" title="Cezary Kucharski">Cezary Kucharski</a>. Lewandowski hired renowned dealmaker <a href="/wiki/Pini_Zahavi" title="Pini Zahavi">Pini Zahavi</a> as his new agent. The hiring of Zahavi was rumoured to be the start of Lewandowski trying to seal a summer move to Real Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On 24 February 2018, Lewandowski played his 250th Bundesliga game against <a href="/wiki/Hertha_BSC" title="Hertha BSC">Hertha BSC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> On 19 May 2018, Lewandowski scored Bayern Munich's only goal in a 31 defeat in the <a href="/wiki/2018_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2018 DFB-Pokal Final">DFB-Pokal Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski finished the season as the Bundesliga's top goalscorer with 29 goals. This was the third time Lewandowski won the Bundesliga's top goalscorer award.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with 41 goals in 48 matches in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201819_season">201819 season</span></h5>
<p>On 1 August 2018, after a summer of transfer speculation, Bayern Munich CEO <a href="/wiki/Karl-Heinz_Rummenigge" title="Karl-Heinz Rummenigge">Karl-Heinz Rummenigge</a>, confirmed in an interview that Lewandowski would not be allowed to leave Bayern Munich at any price. Rummenigge said "Our door remains closed, the top quality we have at Bayern Munich will stay here. With Robert, we clearly want to send a signal to people within and outside the club: Bayern Munich are completely different to other clubs who get weak when certain sums are mentioned"<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 12 August 2018, Lewandowski recorded the first ever hat-trick in the <a href="/wiki/DFL-Supercup" title="DFL-Supercup">German Super Cup</a> against Eintracht Frankfurt in the <a href="/wiki/2018_DFL-Supercup" title="2018 DFL-Supercup">2018 edition</a> as Bayern Munich went on to win the title for the record seventh time.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> He also became the all-time top scorer in the German Super Cup history.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 November 2018, Lewandowski became the third-fastest player to score 50 goals in the Champions League when he scored two goals in a 51 win over <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a>. It took Lewandowski just 77 Champions League matches to reach the milestone.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski finished as the top scorer in the UEFA Champions League group stage with eight goals in six matches.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 9 February 2019, Lewandowski scored in a 31 win over Schalke and in doing so became the first player to score 100 competitive goals at the Allianz Arena. His goal was also his 119th league goal for Bayern Munich which saw him draw level with <a href="/wiki/Roland_Wohlfarth" title="Roland Wohlfarth">Roland Wohlfarth</a> as the club's third-highest goalscorer of all-time.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg/170px-2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg/255px-2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg/340px-2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="5472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2019147195017_2019-05-27_Fussball_1.FC_Kaiserslautern_vs_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_-_Sven_-_1D_X_MK_II_-_2036_-_B70I0336.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>He surpassed Wohlfarth the following month after scoring a brace in a 51 win over Gladbach, with his second goal also seeing him equal <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Pizarro" title="Claudio Pizarro">Claudio Pizarro</a>'s record of 195 league goals for the most Bundesliga goals by a foreign player.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In his very next fixture, he broke Pizarro's record by scoring twice in a 60 win over Wolfsburg.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On 6 April 2019, in the 100th Bundesliga meeting between Bayern Munich and Dortmund, Lewandowski scored twice in a 50 win, with his first goal taking him to 200 goals in the league.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski finished the season as the Bundesliga's top goalscorer with 22 goals for the fourth time.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> On 25 May 2019, he scored a brace as Bayern won <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> 30 in the <a href="/wiki/2019_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2019 DFB-Pokal Final">2019 DFB-Pokal Final</a>. With his goals, he became the all-time top scorer in the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">German Cup</a> finals with six, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a> on five.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski finished the season with 40 goals in 47 matches in all competitions, reaching the 40-goal landmark for the fourth consecutive season, also winning his second domestic double with Bayern.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201920_season">201920 season</span></h5>
<p>On 12 August 2019, Lewandowski scored his first goal of the season when Bayern defeated <a href="/wiki/FC_Energie_Cottbus" title="FC Energie Cottbus">Energie Cottbus</a> 31 in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On 16 August 2019, Lewandowski scored two goals in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Bundesliga" title="201920 Bundesliga">201920 Bundesliga</a> opener against Hertha Berlin. With his goals, Lewandowski set a Bundesliga record for scoring a goal in the season opener for the fifth year in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> On 24 August 2019, Lewandowski scored a hat-trick against Schalke at the <a href="/wiki/Veltins_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Veltins Arena">Veltins Arena</a> as Bayern won 30.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On 29 August 2019, Lewandowski extended his contract at Bayern until 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On 18 September 2019, Lewandowski scored his 200th goal for Bayern in a 30 win against Serbian club <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star Belgrade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201920 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, after scoring his tenth goal of the campaign during a 32 win over SC Paderborn 07, he became the first player in Bundesliga history to achieve double figures for goals scored after the first six match rounds.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski then became the first player in Bundesliga history to score in each of the opening nine, ten and eleven matches of a season, surpassing the record of eight set by <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Emerick_Aubameyang" title="Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang">Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> On 26 November 2019, Lewandowski scored 4 goals in under 15 minutes as Bayern defeated Red Star Belgrade 60 in their reverse fixture and clinched first place in their <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_B" title="201920 UEFA Champions League group stage">Champions League group</a>, setting a new record for fastest time to score four goals in a Champions League match. He also became only the second player ever to score four goals in multiple Champions League matches.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 February 2020, Lewandowski equalled <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>'s record of nine away goals in a season in Europe's top club competition. He did so by scoring a goal in a 30 win against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> On 10 August 2020, Lewandowski scored a brace and provided two assists in a 41 win over Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August, he scored one goal in <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona_2%E2%80%938_FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Barcelona 28 FC Bayern Munich">Bayern's 82 trashing of Barcelona</a> in the quarter-finals; hence, he had scored 14 goals across eight consecutive Champions League matches.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski scored another goal, to be 15 goals in total, in his ninth consecutive Champions League match in Bayern's semifinal win against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> His European scoring streak ended when he failed to score a goal in Bayern's <a href="/wiki/2020_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2020 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League final match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a> on 23 August; nevertheless, Bayern defeated PSG 10, giving Lewandowski his first career Champions League title.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> He also became the second player ever to win the European treble, while being the top scorer in all three competitions, repeating <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>'s achievement with <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">AFC Ajax</a> from the 197172 season, however, Lewandowski was the first to do so as the sole top scorer in all three competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-juni_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juni-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zet_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zet-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="202021_season">202021 season</span></h5>
<p>On 4 October 2020, he scored all four goals in a 43 win against Hertha BSC.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> On 24 October, he scored a hat-trick in a 50 win against Eintracht Frankfurt, to become the first player in Bundesliga to score ten goals in only five matches.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On 16 December, he scored a brace against Wolfsburg to be the third player to pass the 250-goal mark in Bundesliga, after Gerd Müller and <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Fischer" title="Klaus Fischer">Klaus Fischer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After winning the treble with Bayern Munich and his performances in the tournaments,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> he was named <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Men%27s_Player" title="The Best FIFA Men&#39;s Player">The Best FIFA Men's Player</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2020" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2020">2020</a> on 17 December 2020 breaking the duopoly of Cristiano Ronaldo and Lionel Messi winning the award and also becoming the first Polish player to win the award.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 January 2021, Lewandowski became the first player in Bundesliga history to score 21 goals after just 16 games  a new Hinrunde record, beating Gerd Müller's 20 goals during the <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Bundesliga" title="196869 Bundesliga">196869 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> On 8 February, he scored a brace in a 20 win over <a href="/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC" title="Al Ahly SC">Al Ahly</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2020 FIFA Club World Cup">2020 FIFA Club World Cup</a> semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On 11 February, he won FIFA Club World Cup 2020 with <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>. He also was involved in <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Pavard" title="Benjamin Pavard">Pavard's</a> winning goal in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 February 2021, Lewandowski opened the score in a 41 win against <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> in the first leg of the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Champions_League#Round_of_16" title="202021 UEFA Champions League">202021 UEFA Champions League round of 16</a>, reaching his 72nd Champions League goal and surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_(footballer)" title="Raúl (footballer)">Raúl</a> as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers" title="List of UEFA Champions League top scorers">third highest goalscorer</a> in the competition's history.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> On 6 March, he scored his 12th Bundesliga hat-trick in a 42 win over his former club Borussia Dortmund, to reach 31 goals in 23 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> On 13 March, he scored a goal in a 31 away win over Werder Bremen, hence he became the joint-second on the all-time Bundesliga scoring list with 268 goals along with Klaus Fischer.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<p>Lewandowski made three appearances for <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_under-21_football_team" title="Poland national under-21 football team">Poland's U21 team</a>, in friendly matches against England, Belarus and Finland.
</p><p>His debut for the senior national team came on 10 September 2008, three weeks after his 20th birthday, against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> where he came on as a substitute and scored a goal in a 20 away win in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification">2010 FIFA World Cup qualification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82odzimierz_Luba%C5%84ski" title="Wodzimierz Lubaski">Wodzimierz Lubaski</a> scored a goal on his debut for the national team at a younger age than Lewandowski, having been 16 at the time. Lewandowski scored another qualifying goal against the same team on 1 April 2009, in a 100 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2011_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg/180px-Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg/270px-Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg/360px-Robert_Lewandowski_2011_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2011_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski playing for <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a> in November 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Playing in Warsaw in the opening match of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> tournament against <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a>, Lewandowski scored the first goal of the competition after an assist from then Dortmund teammate <a href="/wiki/Jakub_B%C5%82aszczykowski" title="Jakub Baszczykowski">Jakub Baszczykowski</a> and was named <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_Match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the Match">Man of the Match</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> He played in all three games for Poland in the tournament, as the co-hosts crashed out of the group stage with two points earned.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski scored two penalties in the 50 win against San Marino on 26 March 2013 during the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 World Cup qualifying campaign</a>, his first match as <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Later on in the campaign, on 6 September, he scored the equaliser against <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Montenegro national football team">Montenegro</a> in a 11 home draw.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Poland did not qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 World Cup</a> in Brazil.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg/150px-Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg/225px-Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg/300px-Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="465" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lewandowski_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lewandowski playing for Poland at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 7 September 2014, in Poland's first <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifier</a>, away against <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_football_team" title="Gibraltar national football team">Gibraltar</a>, Lewandowski scored his first international hat-trick, netting four goals in a 70 win.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> On 13 June 2015, he scored another hat-trick in Poland's 40 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia</a>, with the three goals scored within the space of four minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> On 8 October, he scored twice in a 22 draw away to <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a>, opening and equalising with the last kick of the game to eliminate the hosts.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Three days later he headed the winner in a 21 victory against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>, qualifying Poland for the tournament finals in France.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski ended the campaign with 13 goals, a joint <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship_qualifying" title="UEFA European Championship qualifying">European Championships qualifying</a> record with <a href="/wiki/David_Healy_(footballer)" title="David Healy (footballer)">David Healy</a>'s tally for <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland</a> in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> in France, Lewandowski did not have a shot on target until the last-16 match against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint-%C3%89tienne" title="Saint-Étienne">Saint-Étienne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Following the 11 draw, he scored his team's first attempt in the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shootout</a> victory that sent them to the quarter-finals for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> In the 100th second of the quarter-final against <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_V%C3%A9lodrome" title="Stade Vélodrome">Stade Vélodrome</a>, he finished <a href="/wiki/Kamil_Grosicki" title="Kamil Grosicki">Kamil Grosicki</a>'s cross to open another 11 draw, and again scored in the shootout although the Poles lost.<sup id="cite_ref-portugal_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portugal-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> At the time of Poland's exit, Lewandowski had suffered more fouls than any other player in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-portugal_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portugal-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 October 2017, Lewandowski scored a hat-trick in a 61 win over <a href="/wiki/Armenia_national_football_team" title="Armenia national football team">Armenia</a> to take his tally to 50 goals for Poland, surpassing the previous record of 48 goals set by <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82odzimierz_Luba%C5%84ski" title="Wodzimierz Lubaski">Wodzimierz Lubaski</a> to become the all-time top scorer for Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> On 8 October 2017, Lewandowski scored a goal in a 42 win over to Montenegro taking his tally to 51 goals for Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesliga_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesliga-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> He finished the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> campaign with 16 total goals, a record for a European World Cup qualifier.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesliga_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesliga-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lewandowski was called up to the 23-man Polish squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Lewandowski played every minute in all three matches, against <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>. Lewandowski did not score a goal as Poland did not qualify for the knockout phase.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>Lewandowski is widely regarded as one of the best strikers in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> An accurate and efficient finisher with his head and both feet, Lewandowski is a prolific goalscorer. A well-rounded <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>, he is said to possess almost all the necessary qualities of a traditional number nine: height, strength, balance, pace, intelligent movement and proficiency with both feet.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Although he primarily operates as a goal-poacher in the penalty area, due to his positional sense, ability to shoot first time, strength in the air, and powerful shot with either foot, his excellent technical skills, quick feet, proficient dribbling, vision, and physique also enable him to hold up the ball with his back to goal and either bring his teammates into play, or win fouls for his team in useful positions; despite often functioning as a lone-<a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Centre-forward" title="Forward (association football)">centre forward</a> or as an out-and-out striker. He has also stood out for his work-rate and defensive contribution off the ball, and is capable of dropping into deeper roles on the pitch, in order to create space for teammates with his movement, or surprise defenders by making late and sudden attacking runs into the area. Lewandowski is an accurate penalty taker and has repeatedly shown coolness and composure on the spot.
